## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and time t (possible external driving). The equation of motion generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator with nonlinear restoring forces, damping, and periodic driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (linear oscillator with periodic drive)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric + symmetric nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v * x**2 + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (position-dependent damping with drive)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Combined nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3 + c4 * cos(c5 * t) (general nonlinear driven system)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) → symmetric potential wells preserving oscillation symmetry
- Even-power position terms (x**2) → asymmetric potential indicating broken spatial symmetry
- Velocity-position coupling terms like v*x**2 → amplitude-dependent damping (Van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force or parametric excitation
- Negative linear damping with positive cubic velocity term (c1*v + c2*v**3 with opposite signs) → self-sustained limit cycle oscillations
- Product of time-periodic function and position (cos(c*t)*x) → parametric resonance mechanism
- Ratio of odd polynomial in x to even polynomial → bounded restoring force with saturation
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system where phase portrait fully characterizes dynamics
- Linear position term sign determines oscillatory (negative coefficient) vs. unstable (positive coefficient) behavior
- Multiple frequency components in driving suggest quasi-periodic or chaotic forcing scenarios

- `x*log(c|x|+1)` logarithmic
- `exp(ct)` exponential in t

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0892421*v³ - 0.725306*v*(1 - x²) - 1.44736*x - 1.44736*x*exp(-|x|)`

Expanding: `-0.0892421*v³ - 0.725306*v + 0.725306*v*x² - 1.44736*x - 1.44736*x*exp(-|x|)`

So the GT has these basis functions:
- `v³` (coeff ≈ -0.0892)
- `v` (coeff ≈ -0.7253)
- `v*x²` (coeff ≈ 0.7253)
- `x` (coeff ≈ -1.4474)
- `x*exp(-|x|)` (coeff ≈ -1.4474)

The key challenge is matching `x*exp(-|x|)`. Let me analyze which candidates could represent this function.

**Key observation:** `x*exp(-|x|)` is a specific function that cannot be exactly represented by:
- `x*exp(c*x²)` (Gaussian-type, symmetric in x differently)
- `x/(x²+1)` or `x/(x²+1)²` (rational functions)
- `x*log(c*|x|+1)` (logarithmic)
- polynomials in x

Let me verify: `x*exp(-|x|)` has specific behavior - it's odd, peaks near x=±1, and decays exponentially. No finite combination of rational functions, polynomials, or logarithmic terms can exactly equal it.

**For each candidate, I need to check if the basis functions can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`:**

- Candidates with `x*exp(c*x²)`: This is `x*exp(c*x²)`, which for c<0 gives a Gaussian bump. This is NOT equal to `x*exp(-|x|)` for any constant c, since `exp(-c*x²) ≠ exp(-|x|)`.

- Candidates with `x*log(c*|x|+1)`: logarithmic, not exponential decay. NOT equivalent.

- Candidates with `x/(x²+1)` and `x/(x²+1)²`: rational functions with algebraic decay, NOT exponential decay.

- Candidates with polynomial terms only: cannot match exponential decay.

- Candidates with `exp(c*t)`, `sin`, `cos`, `log(c*x+1)`: wrong basis functions.

Since `x*exp(-|x|)` is a transcendental function that cannot be exactly represented by any combination of:
- Polynomials in x, v
- Rational functions like `x/(ax²+1)`, `x/(ax²+1)²`
- `x*log(c|x|+1)`
- `x*exp(cx²)`
- Trigonometric functions of t
- `exp(ct)`

**None of these candidates can exactly match the GT.**

Let me double-check Candidate 1 and 10 which have `x*exp(c*x²)`: For this to equal `x*exp(-|x|)`, we'd need `c*x² = -|x|`, i.e., `c = -1/|x|`, which isn't a constant. **No match.**

Candidates with `x*log(c*|x|+1)`: For small |x|, `log(c|x|+1) ≈ c|x|`, giving `c*x*|x|` which is not `x*exp(-|x|)`. **No match.**

Going through all 50 candidates systematically, none contain the basis function `x*exp(-|x|)` or any combination that could produce it exactly.
